<pr_description>
ACIR != Brillig: `pop_back` returns wrong result in Brillig
### Aim

Discovered testing https://github.com/noir-lang/noir/pull/9262

The following program fails in ACIR but returns a wrong result in Brillig:

```rust
global G_A: [Field] = &[-282608142060723387702497189224219065418];
fn main() -> pub Field {
    let (a, _) = G_A.pop_back();
    let (_, f) = a.pop_back();
    f
}
```

### Expected Behavior

They should both fail because the slice has only 1 item, so we can't pop twice.

### Bug

```console
❯ cargo run -q -p nargo_cli -- execute --force-brillig

[fuzz_testing] Witness saved to target/fuzz_testing.gz

❯ cargo run -q -p nargo_cli -- execute --force
error: Index out of bounds, array has size 1, but index was -1

  │
4 │     let (_, f) = a.pop_back();
  │                  ----------
  │
  = Call stack:
    1. src/main.nr:4:18

Failed to solve program: 'Index out of bounds, array has size 1, but index was -1'
```

     1	//! Codegen for converting SSA slice intrinsic functions to Brillig bytecode.
     2	use acvm::acir::brillig::MemoryAddress;
     3	
     4	use crate::brillig::brillig_ir::{
     5	    BrilligBinaryOp,
     6	    brillig_variable::{BrilligVariable, BrilligVector, SingleAddrVariable},
     7	    registers::RegisterAllocator,
     8	};
     9	
    10	use super::super::brillig_block::BrilligBlock;
    11	
    12	impl<Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligBlock<'_, Registers> {
    13	    /// Take a list of [BrilligVariable] and copy the memory they point at to the `write_pointer`,
    14	    /// increasing the address by 1 between each variable.
    15	    fn write_variables(&mut self, write_pointer: MemoryAddress, variables: &[BrilligVariable]) {
    16	        for (index, variable) in variables.iter().enumerate() {
    17	            self.brillig_context.store_instruction(write_pointer, variable.extract_register());
    18	            if index != variables.len() - 1 {
    19	                self.brillig_context.codegen_usize_op_in_place(
    20	                    write_pointer,
    21	                    BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
    22	                    1,
    23	                );
    24	            }
    25	        }
    26	    }
    27	
    28	    /// Prepare a vector for pushing a number of new (flattened) items to the back,
    29	    /// then write those variables to the returned write pointer.
    30	    pub(crate) fn slice_push_back_operation(
    31	        &mut self,
    32	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
    33	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    34	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    35	        variables_to_insert: &[BrilligVariable],
    36	    ) {
    37	        let write_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
    38	        self.brillig_context.call_prepare_vector_push_procedure(
    39	            source_len,
    40	            source_vector,
    41	            target_vector,
    42	            *write_pointer,
    43	            variables_to_insert.len(),
    44	            true,
    45	        );
    46	
    47	        self.write_variables(*write_pointer, variables_to_insert);
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    /// Prepare a vector for pushing a number of new (flattened) items to the front,
    51	    /// then write those variables to the returned write pointer.
    52	    pub(crate) fn slice_push_front_operation(
    53	        &mut self,
    54	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
    55	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    56	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    57	        variables_to_insert: &[BrilligVariable],
    58	    ) {
    59	        let write_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
    60	        self.brillig_context.call_prepare_vector_push_procedure(
    61	            source_len,
    62	            source_vector,
    63	            target_vector,
    64	            *write_pointer,
    65	            variables_to_insert.len(),
    66	            false,
    67	        );
    68	
    69	        self.write_variables(*write_pointer, variables_to_insert);
    70	    }
    71	
    72	    /// Read the memory starting at the pointer into successive variables.
    73	    fn read_variables(&mut self, read_pointer: MemoryAddress, variables: &[BrilligVariable]) {
    74	        for (index, variable) in variables.iter().enumerate() {
    75	            self.brillig_context.load_instruction(variable.extract_register(), read_pointer);
    76	            if index != variables.len() - 1 {
    77	                self.brillig_context.codegen_usize_op_in_place(
    78	                    read_pointer,
    79	                    BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
    80	                    1,
    81	                );
    82	            }
    83	        }
    84	    }
    85	
    86	    /// Read the popped number of variables from the front of the source vector,
    87	    /// then create the target vector from the source by skipping the number of popped items.
    88	    pub(crate) fn slice_pop_front_operation(
    89	        &mut self,
    90	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
    91	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    92	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    93	        removed_items: &[BrilligVariable],
    94	    ) {
    95	        let read_pointer = self.brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
    96	        self.read_variables(*read_pointer, removed_items);
    97	
    98	        self.brillig_context.call_vector_pop_front_procedure(
    99	            source_len,
   100	            source_vector,
   101	            target_vector,
   102	            removed_items.len(),
   103	        );
   104	    }
   105	
   106	    /// Create new vector with a number of (flattened) items popped from the back,
   107	    /// then read the popped items into the variables representing the removed items.
   108	    pub(crate) fn slice_pop_back_operation(
   109	        &mut self,
   110	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
   111	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
   112	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
   113	        removed_items: &[BrilligVariable],
   114	    ) {
   115	        let read_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
   116	        self.brillig_context.call_vector_pop_back_procedure(
   117	            source_len,
   118	            source_vector,
   119	            target_vector,
   120	            *read_pointer,
   121	            removed_items.len(),
   122	        );
   123	
   124	        self.read_variables(*read_pointer, removed_items);
   125	    }
   126	
   127	    /// Prepare a vector for inserting a number of (flattened) items at a specific index
   128	    /// by making a hole for them, then write the variables to the returned write pointer.
   129	    pub(crate) fn slice_insert_operation(
   130	        &mut self,
   131	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
   132	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
   133	        index: SingleAddrVariable,
   134	        items: &[BrilligVariable],
   135	    ) {
   136	        let write_pointer = self.brillig_context.allocate_register();
   137	
   138	        self.brillig_context.call_prepare_vector_insert_procedure(
   139	            source_vector,
   140	            target_vector,
   141	            index,
   142	            *write_pointer,
   143	            items.len(),
   144	        );
   145	
   146	        self.write_variables(*write_pointer, items);
   147	    }
   148	
   149	    /// Read a number of (flattened) items at a specific index of a vector into the variables
   150	    /// representing the removed items, then create a new vector with the same number of
   151	    /// items removed and subsequent items shifted to the left.
   152	    pub(crate) fn slice_remove_operation(
   153	        &mut self,
   154	        target_vector: BrilligVector,
   155	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
   156	        index: SingleAddrVariable,
   157	        removed_items: &[BrilligVariable],
   158	    ) {
   159	        let read_pointer = self.brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
   160	        self.brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   161	            *read_pointer,
   162	            index.address,
   163	            *read_pointer,
   164	            BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   165	        );
   166	        self.read_variables(*read_pointer, removed_items);
   167	
   168	        self.brillig_context.call_vector_remove_procedure(
   169	            source_vector,
   170	            target_vector,
   171	            index,
   172	            removed_items.len(),
   173	        );
   174	    }
   175	}

   244	                // The input size semantic length.
   245	                BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(BRILLIG_MEMORY_ADDRESSING_BIT_SIZE),
   246	                // The input slice of the array items, with a known size/capacity.
   247	                BrilligParameter::Slice(
   248	                    vec![BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(BRILLIG_MEMORY_ADDRESSING_BIT_SIZE)],
   249	                    source.len(),
   250	                ),
   251	                // The item to push.
   252	                BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(BRILLIG_MEMORY_ADDRESSING_BIT_SIZE),
   253	            ];
   254	            // We expect 1 item to be pushed. The capacity might be more, depending on reuse.
   255	            let result_length = source_len + 1;
   256	            assert_eq!(
   257	                result_length,
   258	                expected_return.len(),
   259	                "expected return data should be 1 longer than the input"
   260	            );
   261	            // Returned data expected to be leading with length and capacity, followed by the items.
   262	            let result_length_with_metadata = result_length + 2;
   263	
   264	            // Entry points don't support returning slices, so we implicitly cast the vector to an array
   265	            // With the metadata at the start.
   266	            let returns = vec![BrilligParameter::Array(
   267	                vec![BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(BRILLIG_MEMORY_ADDRESSING_BIT_SIZE)],

   287	                &hoisted_globals,
   288	            );
   289

   291	                block.slice_push_back_operation(
   292	                    *target_vector,
   293	                    *source_len_var,
   294	                    *source_vector,
   295	                    &[item_to_insert.to_var()],
   296	                );
   297	            } else {

   303	                );
   304	            }

   306	            context.codegen_return(&[target_vector.to_var()]);

   313

   315	            let (vm, return_data_offset, return_data_size) = create_and_run_vm(inputs, &bytecode);

     1	use acvm::{AcirField, acir::brillig::MemoryAddress};
     2	
     3	use super::ProcedureId;
     4	use crate::brillig::brillig_ir::{
     5	    BrilligBinaryOp, BrilligContext,
     6	    brillig_variable::{BrilligVector, SingleAddrVariable},
     7	    debug_show::DebugToString,
     8	    registers::{RegisterAllocator, ScratchSpace},
     9	};
    10	
    11	impl<F: AcirField + DebugToString, Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligContext<F, Registers> {
    12	    /// Copy arguments to [ScratchSpace] and call [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    13	    ///
    14	    /// Pops `item_pop_count` items from the back of a `source_vector`, returning the new `destination_vector`
    15	    /// and the pointer to the popped items in `read_pointer`.
    16	    ///
    17	    /// The `item_pop_count` equals the number of variables to pop into in SSA.
    18	    /// The `source_len` is the semantic (not flattened) length of the vector.
    19	    pub(crate) fn call_vector_pop_back_procedure(
    20	        &mut self,
    21	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    22	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    23	        destination_vector: BrilligVector,
    24	        read_pointer: MemoryAddress,
    25	        item_pop_count: usize,
    26	    ) {
    27	        let [
    28	            source_vector_length_arg,
    29	            source_vector_pointer_arg,
    30	            item_pop_count_arg,
    31	            destination_vector_pointer_return,
    32	            read_pointer_return,
    33	        ] = self.make_scratch_registers();
    34	
    35	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_length_arg, source_len.address);
    36	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_pointer_arg, source_vector.pointer);
    37	        self.usize_const_instruction(item_pop_count_arg, item_pop_count.into());
    38	
    39	        self.add_procedure_call_instruction(ProcedureId::VectorPopBack);
    40	
    41	        self.mov_instruction(destination_vector.pointer, destination_vector_pointer_return);
    42	        self.mov_instruction(read_pointer, read_pointer_return);
    43	    }
    44	}
    45	
    46	/// Compile [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    47	pub(super) fn compile_vector_pop_back_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
    48	    brillig_context: &mut BrilligContext<F, ScratchSpace>,
    49	) {
    50	    let [
    51	        source_vector_length_arg,
    52	        source_vector_pointer_arg,
    53	        item_pop_count_arg,
    54	        destination_vector_pointer_return,
    55	        read_pointer_return,
    56	    ] = brillig_context.allocate_scratch_registers();
    57	
    58	    let source_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: source_vector_pointer_arg };
    59	    let target_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: destination_vector_pointer_return };
    60	
    61	    // First we need to allocate the target vector decrementing the size by `item_pop_count`.
    62	    // We use the semantic length, rather than load the vector size from the meta-data,
    63	    // because after merging vectors of different lengths, the semantic length can be different
    64	    // then the number of items in the vector, which is the longer of the merged values.
    65	    let source_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    66	    brillig_context.codegen_vector_flattened_size(
    67	        source_size.address,
    68	        source_vector_length_arg,
    69	        item_pop_count_arg,
    70	    );
    71	
    72	    // We will pop a number of (flattened) items; targets_size = source_size - item_pop_count
    73	    let target_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    74	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    75	        source_size.address,
    76	        item_pop_count_arg,
    77	        target_size.address,
    78	        BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    79	    );
    80	
    81	    let rc = brillig_context.codegen_read_vector_rc(source_vector);
    82	
    83	    let is_rc_one = brillig_context.codegen_usize_equals_one(*rc);
    84	
    85	    let source_vector_items_pointer =
    86	        brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
    87	
    88	    brillig_context.codegen_branch(is_rc_one.address, |brillig_context, is_rc_one| {
    89	        if is_rc_one {
    90	            // We can reuse the source vector, updating its length
    91	            brillig_context.mov_instruction(target_vector.pointer, source_vector.pointer);
    92	            brillig_context.codegen_update_vector_size(target_vector, *target_size);
    93	        } else {
    94	            // We need to clone the source vector; allocate memory for it.
    95	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector(target_vector, *target_size, None);
    96	
    97	            let target_vector_items_pointer =
    98	                brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(target_vector);
    99	
   100	            // Now we copy the source vector starting at index 0 into the target vector but with the reduced length.
   101	            brillig_context.codegen_mem_copy(
   102	                *source_vector_items_pointer,
   103	                *target_vector_items_pointer,
   104	                *target_size,
   105	            );
   106	
   107	            // We don't decrease the RC of the source vector, otherwise repeatedly popping the same item
   108	            // from the original (immutable) handle would bring its RC down to 1.
   109	        }
   110	    });
   111	
   112	    // Finally set the pointer where the popped items can be read from to the source vector.
   113	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   114	        *source_vector_items_pointer,
   115	        target_size.address,
   116	        read_pointer_return,
   117	        BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   118	    );
   119	}

     1	use acvm::{AcirField, acir::brillig::MemoryAddress};
     2	
     3	use super::ProcedureId;
     4	use crate::brillig::brillig_ir::{
     5	    BrilligBinaryOp, BrilligContext,
     6	    brillig_variable::{BrilligVector, SingleAddrVariable},
     7	    debug_show::DebugToString,
     8	    registers::{RegisterAllocator, ScratchSpace},
     9	};
    10	
    11	impl<F: AcirField + DebugToString, Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligContext<F, Registers> {
    12	    /// Copy arguments to [ScratchSpace] and call [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    13	    ///
    14	    /// Pops `item_pop_count` items from the back of a `source_vector`, returning the new `destination_vector`
    15	    /// and the pointer to the popped items in `read_pointer`.
    16	    ///
    17	    /// The `item_pop_count` equals the number of variables to pop into in SSA.
    18	    /// The `source_len` is the semantic (not flattened) length of the vector.
    19	    pub(crate) fn call_vector_pop_back_procedure(
    20	        &mut self,
    21	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    22	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    23	        destination_vector: BrilligVector,
    24	        read_pointer: MemoryAddress,
    25	        item_pop_count: usize,
    26	    ) {
    27	        let [
    28	            source_vector_length_arg,
    29	            source_vector_pointer_arg,
    30	            item_pop_count_arg,
    31	            destination_vector_pointer_return,
    32	            read_pointer_return,
    33	        ] = self.make_scratch_registers();
    34	
    35	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_length_arg, source_len.address);
    36	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_pointer_arg, source_vector.pointer);
    37	        self.usize_const_instruction(item_pop_count_arg, item_pop_count.into());
    38	
    39	        self.add_procedure_call_instruction(ProcedureId::VectorPopBack);
    40	
    41	        self.mov_instruction(destination_vector.pointer, destination_vector_pointer_return);
    42	        self.mov_instruction(read_pointer, read_pointer_return);
    43	    }
    44	}
    45	
    46	/// Compile [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    47	pub(super) fn compile_vector_pop_back_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
    48	    brillig_context: &mut BrilligContext<F, ScratchSpace>,
    49	) {
    50	    let [
    51	        source_vector_length_arg,
    52	        source_vector_pointer_arg,
    53	        item_pop_count_arg,
    54	        destination_vector_pointer_return,
    55	        read_pointer_return,
    56	    ] = brillig_context.allocate_scratch_registers();
    57	
    58	    let source_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: source_vector_pointer_arg };
    59	    let target_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: destination_vector_pointer_return };
    60	
    61	    // First we need to allocate the target vector decrementing the size by `item_pop_count`.
    62	    // We use the semantic length, rather than load the vector size from the meta-data,
    63	    // because after merging vectors of different lengths, the semantic length can be different
    64	    // then the number of items in the vector, which is the longer of the merged values.
    65	    let source_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    66	    brillig_context.codegen_vector_flattened_size(
    67	        source_size.address,
    68	        source_vector_length_arg,
    69	        item_pop_count_arg,
    70	    );
    71	
    72	    // We will pop a number of (flattened) items; targets_size = source_size - item_pop_count
    73	    let target_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    74	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    75	        source_size.address,
    76	        item_pop_count_arg,
    77	        target_size.address,
    78	        BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    79	    );
    80	
    81	    let rc = brillig_context.codegen_read_vector_rc(source_vector);
    82	
    83	    let is_rc_one = brillig_context.codegen_usize_equals_one(*rc);
    84	
    85	    let source_vector_items_pointer =
    86	        brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
    87	
    88	    brillig_context.codegen_branch(is_rc_one.address, |brillig_context, is_rc_one| {
    89	        if is_rc_one {
    90	            // We can reuse the source vector, updating its length
    91	            brillig_context.mov_instruction(target_vector.pointer, source_vector.pointer);
    92	            brillig_context.codegen_update_vector_size(target_vector, *target_size);
    93	        } else {
    94	            // We need to clone the source vector; allocate memory for it.
    95	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector(target_vector, *target_size, None);
    96	
    97	            let target_vector_items_pointer =
    98	                brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(target_vector);
    99	
   100	            // Now we copy the source vector starting at index 0 into the target vector but with the reduced length.
   101	            brillig_context.codegen_mem_copy(
   102	                *source_vector_items_pointer,
   103	                *target_vector_items_pointer,
   104	                *target_size,
   105	            );
   106	
   107	            // We don't decrease the RC of the source vector, otherwise repeatedly popping the same item
   108	            // from the original (immutable) handle would bring its RC down to 1.
   109	        }
   110	    });
   111	
   112	    // Finally set the pointer where the popped items can be read from to the source vector.
   113	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   114	        *source_vector_items_pointer,
   115	        target_size.address,
   116	        read_pointer_return,
   117	        BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   118	    );
   119	}
   120

   213	    /// Emit opcodes to reverse the order of the `size` elements pointed by `pointer`.
   214	    ///
   215	    /// It is the responsibility of the caller to ensure that the ref-count of the array is 1.
   216	    pub(crate) fn codegen_array_reverse(
   217	        &mut self,
   218	        items_pointer: MemoryAddress,
   219	        size: MemoryAddress,
   220	    ) {
   221	        if self.can_call_procedures {
   222	            self.call_array_reverse_procedure(items_pointer, size);
   223	            return;
   224	        }
   225	
   226	        // for i in 0..size/2 { swap(items[i], items[size-1-i]); }
   227	        let iteration_count = self.allocate_register();
   228	        self.codegen_usize_op(size, *iteration_count, BrilligBinaryOp::UnsignedDiv, 2);
   229	
   230	        let start_value_register = self.allocate_register();
   231	        let end_value_register = self.allocate_register();
   232	        let index_at_end = self.allocate_register();
   233	
   234	        // The index going from back to front.
   235	        self.mov_instruction(*index_at_end, size);
   236	
   237	        self.codegen_loop(*iteration_count, |ctx, iterator_register| {
   238	            // The index at the end of the array is size - 1 - iterator
   239	            ctx.codegen_usize_op_in_place(*index_at_end, BrilligBinaryOp::Sub, 1);
   240	            let index_at_end_var = SingleAddrVariable::new_usize(*index_at_end);
   241	
   242	            // Load both values
   243	            ctx.codegen_load_with_offset(items_pointer, iterator_register, *start_value_register);
   244	            ctx.codegen_load_with_offset(items_pointer, index_at_end_var, *end_value_register);
   245	
   246	            // Write both values
   247	            ctx.codegen_store_with_offset(items_pointer, iterator_register, *end_value_register);
   248	            ctx.codegen_store_with_offset(items_pointer, index_at_end_var, *start_value_register);
   249	        });
   250	    }

     1	use acvm::{AcirField, acir::brillig::MemoryAddress};
     2	
     3	use super::ProcedureId;
     4	use crate::brillig::brillig_ir::{
     5	    BrilligBinaryOp, BrilligContext,
     6	    brillig_variable::{BrilligVector, SingleAddrVariable},
     7	    debug_show::DebugToString,
     8	    registers::{RegisterAllocator, ScratchSpace},
     9	};
    10	
    11	impl<F: AcirField + DebugToString, Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligContext<F, Registers> {
    12	    /// Copy arguments to [ScratchSpace] and call [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    13	    ///
    14	    /// Pops `item_pop_count` items from the back of a `source_vector`, returning the new `destination_vector`
    15	    /// and the pointer to the popped items in `read_pointer`.
    16	    ///
    17	    /// The `item_pop_count` equals the number of variables to pop into in SSA.
    18	    /// The `source_len` is the semantic (not flattened) length of the vector.
    19	    pub(crate) fn call_vector_pop_back_procedure(
    20	        &mut self,
    21	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    22	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    23	        destination_vector: BrilligVector,
    24	        read_pointer: MemoryAddress,
    25	        item_pop_count: usize,
    26	    ) {
    27	        let [
    28	            source_vector_length_arg,
    29	            source_vector_pointer_arg,
    30	            item_pop_count_arg,
    31	            destination_vector_pointer_return,
    32	            read_pointer_return,
    33	        ] = self.make_scratch_registers();
    34	
    35	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_length_arg, source_len.address);
    36	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_pointer_arg, source_vector.pointer);
    37	        self.usize_const_instruction(item_pop_count_arg, item_pop_count.into());
    38	
    39	        self.add_procedure_call_instruction(ProcedureId::VectorPopBack);
    40	
    41	        self.mov_instruction(destination_vector.pointer, destination_vector_pointer_return);
    42	        self.mov_instruction(read_pointer, read_pointer_return);
    43	    }
    44	}
    45	
    46	/// Compile [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    47	pub(super) fn compile_vector_pop_back_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
    48	    brillig_context: &mut BrilligContext<F, ScratchSpace>,
    49	) {
    50	    let [
    51	        source_vector_length_arg,
    52	        source_vector_pointer_arg,
    53	        item_pop_count_arg,
    54	        destination_vector_pointer_return,
    55	        read_pointer_return,
    56	    ] = brillig_context.allocate_scratch_registers();
    57	
    58	    let source_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: source_vector_pointer_arg };
    59	    let target_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: destination_vector_pointer_return };
    60	
    61	    // First we need to allocate the target vector decrementing the size by `item_pop_count`.
    62	    // We use the semantic length, rather than load the vector size from the meta-data,
    63	    // because after merging vectors of different lengths, the semantic length can be different
    64	    // then the number of items in the vector, which is the longer of the merged values.
    65	    let source_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    66	    brillig_context.codegen_vector_flattened_size(
    67	        source_size.address,
    68	        source_vector_length_arg,
    69	        item_pop_count_arg,
    70	    );
    71	
    72	    // We will pop a number of (flattened) items; targets_size = source_size - item_pop_count
    73	    let target_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    74	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    75	        source_size.address,
    76	        item_pop_count_arg,
    77	        target_size.address,
    78	        BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    79	    );
    80	
    81	    let rc = brillig_context.codegen_read_vector_rc(source_vector);
    82	
    83	    let is_rc_one = brillig_context.codegen_usize_equals_one(*rc);
    84	
    85	    let source_vector_items_pointer =
    86	        brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
    87	
    88	    brillig_context.codegen_branch(is_rc_one.address, |brillig_context, is_rc_one| {
    89	        if is_rc_one {
    90	            // We can reuse the source vector, updating its length
    91	            brillig_context.mov_instruction(target_vector.pointer, source_vector.pointer);
    92	            brillig_context.codegen_update_vector_size(target_vector, *target_size);
    93	        } else {
    94	            // We need to clone the source vector; allocate memory for it.
    95	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector(target_vector, *target_size, None);
    96	
    97	            let target_vector_items_pointer =
    98	                brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(target_vector);
    99	
   100	            // Now we copy the source vector starting at index 0 into the target vector but with the reduced length.
   101	            brillig_context.codegen_mem_copy(
   102	                *source_vector_items_pointer,
   103	                *target_vector_items_pointer,
   104	                *target_size,
   105	            );
   106	
   107	            // We don't decrease the RC of the source vector, otherwise repeatedly popping the same item
   108	            // from the original (immutable) handle would bring its RC down to 1.
   109	        }
   110	    });
   111	
   112	    // Finally set the pointer where the popped items can be read from to the source vector.
   113	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   114	        *source_vector_items_pointer,
   115	        target_size.address,
   116	        read_pointer_return,
   117	        BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   118	    );
   119	}
   120

    36	/// Procedures are a set of complex operations that are common in the noir language.
    37	/// Extracting them to reusable procedures allows us to reduce the size of the generated Brillig.
    38	/// Procedures receive their arguments on scratch space to avoid stack dumping&restoring.
    39	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Eq, PartialEq, Hash, PartialOrd, Ord, Deserialize, Serialize)]
    40	pub enum ProcedureId {
    41	    /// Conditionally copies a source array to a destination array.
    42	    /// If the reference count of the source array is 1, then we can directly copy the pointer of the source array to the destination array.
    43	    ArrayCopy,
    44	    /// Reverses an array in-place.
    45	    /// It is the responsibility of the caller to ensure the reference count of the array is 1.
    46	    ArrayReverse,
    47	    /// Conditionally copies a source vector to a destination vector.
    48	    /// If the reference count of the source vector is 1, then we can directly copy the pointer of the source vector to the destination vector.
    49	    VectorCopy,
    50	    /// Copy a number of items between two heap addresses.
    51	    MemCopy,
    52	    /// Prepares a vector for pushing a new item. It tries to reuse the source vector,
    53	    /// allocating a new vector with a higher capacity and the copy of the source vector items if necessary.
    54	    ///
    55	    /// If the parameter is `true` it pushes to the back, otherwise to the front.
    56	    PrepareVectorPush(bool),
    57	    /// Pops items from the front of a vector, returning the new vector.
    58	    /// Reuses the source vector if the reference count is 1.
    59	    VectorPopFront,
    60	    /// Pops items from the back of a vector, returning the new vector and the pointer to the popped items.
    61	    /// Reuses the source vector if the reference count is 1.
    62	    VectorPopBack,
    63	    /// Prepare a vector for a insert operation, leaving a hole at the index position, returning a pointer where the item can be written.
    64	    PrepareVectorInsert,
    65	    /// Remove items at a given index from a vector, returning the new vector.
    66	    /// Reuses the source vector if the reference count is 1.
    67	    VectorRemove,
    68	    /// Check that the stack memory has not exceeded the maximum size allowed by the layout.
    69	    CheckMaxStackDepth,
    70	    /// Revert with the given error message.
    71	    RevertWithString(String),
    72	}
    73	
    74	impl ProcedureId {
    75	    pub(crate) fn to_debug_id(&self) -> ProcedureDebugId {
    76	        ProcedureDebugId(match self {
    77	            ProcedureId::ArrayCopy => 0,
    78	            ProcedureId::ArrayReverse => 1,
    79	            ProcedureId::VectorCopy => 2,
    80	            ProcedureId::MemCopy => 3,
    81	            ProcedureId::PrepareVectorPush(true) => 4,
    82	            ProcedureId::PrepareVectorPush(false) => 5,
    83	            ProcedureId::VectorPopFront => 6,
    84	            ProcedureId::VectorPopBack => 7,
    85	            ProcedureId::PrepareVectorInsert => 8,
    86	            ProcedureId::VectorRemove => 9,
    87	            ProcedureId::CheckMaxStackDepth => 10,
    88	            ProcedureId::RevertWithString(_) => 11,
    89	        })
    90	    }
    91	
    92	    pub fn from_debug_id(debug_id: ProcedureDebugId) -> Self {
    93	        let inner = debug_id.0;
    94	        match inner {
    95	            0 => ProcedureId::ArrayCopy,
    96	            1 => ProcedureId::ArrayReverse,
    97	            2 => ProcedureId::VectorCopy,
    98	            3 => ProcedureId::MemCopy,
    99	            4 => ProcedureId::PrepareVectorPush(true),
   100	            5 => ProcedureId::PrepareVectorPush(false),
   101	            6 => ProcedureId::VectorPopFront,
   102	            7 => ProcedureId::VectorPopBack,
   103	            8 => ProcedureId::PrepareVectorInsert,
   104	            9 => ProcedureId::VectorRemove,
   105	            10 => ProcedureId::CheckMaxStackDepth,
   106	            11 => ProcedureId::RevertWithString("".to_string()),
   107	            _ => panic!("Unsupported procedure debug ID of {inner} was supplied"),
   108	        }
   109	    }
   110	}
   111	
   112	impl std::fmt::Display for ProcedureId {
   113	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter<'_>) -> std::fmt::Result {
   114	        match self {
   115	            ProcedureId::ArrayCopy => write!(f, "ArrayCopy"),
   116	            ProcedureId::ArrayReverse => write!(f, "ArrayReverse"),
   117	            ProcedureId::VectorCopy => write!(f, "VectorCopy"),
   118	            ProcedureId::MemCopy => write!(f, "MemCopy"),
   119	            ProcedureId::PrepareVectorPush(flag) => write!(f, "PrepareVectorPush({flag})"),
   120	            ProcedureId::VectorPopFront => write!(f, "VectorPopFront"),
   121	            ProcedureId::VectorPopBack => write!(f, "VectorPopBack"),
   122	            ProcedureId::PrepareVectorInsert => write!(f, "PrepareVectorInsert"),
   123	            ProcedureId::VectorRemove => write!(f, "VectorRemove"),
   124	            ProcedureId::CheckMaxStackDepth => write!(f, "CheckMaxStackDepth"),
   125	            ProcedureId::RevertWithString(_) => write!(f, "ErrorWithString"),
   126	        }
   127	    }
   128	}

   130	/// Compile a procedure as a stand-alone Brillig artifact, generating byte code for a specific operation,
   131	/// reading and returning arguments through the [ScratchSpace][crate::brillig::brillig_ir::registers::ScratchSpace].
   132	pub(crate) fn compile_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
   133	    procedure_id: ProcedureId,
   134	    options: &BrilligOptions,
   135	    stack_start: usize,
   136	) -> BrilligArtifact<F> {
   137	    let mut brillig_context = BrilligContext::new_for_procedure(procedure_id.clone(), options);
   138	    brillig_context.enter_context(Label::procedure(procedure_id.clone()));
   139	
   140	    match procedure_id {
   141	        ProcedureId::MemCopy => compile_mem_copy_procedure(&mut brillig_context),
   142	        ProcedureId::ArrayCopy => compile_array_copy_procedure(&mut brillig_context),
   143	        ProcedureId::ArrayReverse => compile_array_reverse_procedure(&mut brillig_context),
   144	        ProcedureId::VectorCopy => compile_vector_copy_procedure(&mut brillig_context),
   145	        ProcedureId::PrepareVectorPush(push_back) => {
   146	            compile_prepare_vector_push_procedure(&mut brillig_context, push_back);
   147	        }
   148	        ProcedureId::VectorPopFront => {
   149	            compile_vector_pop_front_procedure(&mut brillig_context);
   150	        }
   151	        ProcedureId::VectorPopBack => {
   152	            compile_vector_pop_back_procedure(&mut brillig_context);
   153	        }
   154	        ProcedureId::PrepareVectorInsert => {
   155	            compile_prepare_vector_insert_procedure(&mut brillig_context);
   156	        }
   157	        ProcedureId::VectorRemove => compile_vector_remove_procedure(&mut brillig_context),
   158	        ProcedureId::CheckMaxStackDepth => {
   159	            compile_check_max_stack_depth_procedure(&mut brillig_context, stack_start);
   160	        }
   161	        ProcedureId::RevertWithString(error_string) => {
   162	            compile_error_with_string_procedure(&mut brillig_context, error_string);
   163	        }
   164	    };
   165	
   166	    brillig_context.return_instruction();
   167	    brillig_context.into_artifact()
   168	}

     2	
     3	use super::ProcedureId;
     4	use crate::{
     5	    brillig::brillig_ir::{
     6	        BrilligContext, ReservedRegisters,
     7	        debug_show::DebugToString,
     8	        registers::{RegisterAllocator, ScratchSpace},
     9	    },

    11	};
    12	
    13	impl<F: AcirField + DebugToString, Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligContext<F, Registers> {
    14	    /// Reverts with the error selector of the given string
    15	    /// This procedure is useful to deduplicate generating code for the same selector.
    16	    pub(crate) fn call_error_with_string_procedure(&mut self, error_string: String) {
    17	        self.add_procedure_call_instruction(ProcedureId::RevertWithString(error_string));
    18	    }
    19	}
    20	
    21	pub(super) fn compile_error_with_string_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
    22	    brillig_context: &mut BrilligContext<F, ScratchSpace>,
    23	    error_string: String,
    24	) {
    25	    // Compute the error selector and register the error type
    26	    let error_type = ErrorType::String(error_string);
    27	    let error_selector = error_type.selector();
    28	    brillig_context.obj.error_types.insert(error_selector, error_type);
    29	
    30	    // Write the selector to the free memory pointer and trap with it as revert data
    31	    brillig_context.indirect_const_instruction(
    32	        ReservedRegisters::free_memory_pointer(),
    33	        64,
    34	        u128::from(error_selector.as_u64()).into(),
    35	    );
    36	    brillig_context.trap_instruction(HeapVector {
    37	        pointer: ReservedRegisters::free_memory_pointer(),
    38	        size: ReservedRegisters::usize_one(),
    39	    });
    40	}

    19	impl<F: AcirField + DebugToString, Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligContext<F, Registers> {
    20	    pub(crate) fn codegen_generic_iteration<T>(
    21	        &mut self,
    22	        make_iterator: impl FnOnce(&mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>) -> T,
    23	        update_iterator: impl FnOnce(&mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>, &T),
    24	        make_finish_condition: impl FnOnce(
    25	            &mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>,
    26	            &T,
    27	        ) -> Allocated<SingleAddrVariable, Registers>,
    28	        on_iteration: impl FnOnce(&mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>, &T),
    29	        clean_iterator: impl FnOnce(&mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>, T),
    30	    ) {
    31	        let iterator = make_iterator(self);
    32	
    33	        let (loop_section, loop_label) = self.reserve_next_section_label();
    34	        self.enter_section(loop_section);
    35	
    36	        // Loop body
    37	        let should_end = make_finish_condition(self, &iterator);
    38	
    39	        let (exit_loop_section, exit_loop_label) = self.reserve_next_section_label();
    40	
    41	        self.jump_if_instruction(should_end.address, exit_loop_label);
    42	
    43	        // Call the on iteration function
    44	        on_iteration(self, &iterator);
    45	
    46	        // Update iterator
    47	        update_iterator(self, &iterator);
    48	        self.jump_instruction(loop_label);
    49	
    50	        // Exit the loop
    51	        self.enter_section(exit_loop_section);
    52	
    53	        // Free any resources held by the iterator.
    54	        clean_iterator(self, iterator);
    55	    }
    56	
    57	    /// This codegen will issue a loop for (let iterator_register = loop_start; i < loop_bound; i += step)
    58	    /// The body of the loop should be issued by the caller in the on_iteration closure.
    59	    pub(crate) fn codegen_for_loop(
    60	        &mut self,
    61	        loop_start: Option<MemoryAddress>,
    62	        loop_bound: MemoryAddress,
    63	        step: Option<MemoryAddress>,
    64	        on_iteration: impl FnOnce(&mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>, SingleAddrVariable),
    65	    ) {
    66	        let step_register = step.unwrap_or(ReservedRegisters::usize_one());
    67	
    68	        self.codegen_generic_iteration(
    69	            // 1. make_iterator: Initialize counter
    70	            |ctx| {
    71	                if let Some(loop_start) = loop_start {
    72	                    let iterator = ctx.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    73	                    ctx.mov_instruction(iterator.address, loop_start);
    74	                    iterator
    75	                } else {
    76	                    ctx.make_usize_constant_instruction(0_usize.into())
    77	                }
    78	            },
    79	            // 2. update_iterator: Add step
    80	            |ctx, iterator| {
    81	                ctx.memory_op_instruction(
    82	                    iterator.address,
    83	                    step_register,
    84	                    iterator.address,
    85	                    BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
    86	                );
    87	            },
    88	            // 3. make_finish_condition: Check bound <= iterator
    89	            |ctx, iterator| {
    90	                let reached_bound = ctx.allocate_single_addr_bool();
    91	                ctx.memory_op_instruction(
    92	                    loop_bound,
    93	                    iterator.address,
    94	                    reached_bound.address,
    95	                    BrilligBinaryOp::LessThanEquals,
    96	                );
    97	                reached_bound
    98	            },
    99	            // 4. on_iteration: Call user's closure
   100	            |ctx, iterator| {
   101	                on_iteration(ctx, **iterator);
   102	            },
   103	            // 5. clean_iterator: Nothing to clean (auto-deallocated)
   104	            |_, _| {},
   105	        );
   106	    }
   107	
   108	    /// This codegen will issue a loop that will iterate from 0 to iteration_count
   109	    /// The body of the loop should be issued by the caller in the on_iteration closure.
   110	    pub(crate) fn codegen_loop(
   111	        &mut self,
   112	        iteration_count: MemoryAddress,
   113	        on_iteration: impl FnOnce(&mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>, SingleAddrVariable),
   114	    ) {
   115	        self.codegen_for_loop(None, iteration_count, None, on_iteration);
   116	    }
   117	
   118	    /// This codegen will issue an if-then branch that will check if the condition is true
   119	    /// and if so, perform the instructions given in `f(self, true)` and otherwise perform the
   120	    /// instructions given in `f(self, false)`. A boolean is passed instead of two separate
   121	    /// functions to allow the given function to mutably alias its environment.
   122	    pub(crate) fn codegen_branch(
   123	        &mut self,
   124	        condition: MemoryAddress,
   125	        mut f: impl FnMut(&mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>, bool),
   126	    ) {
   127	        // Reserve 3 sections
   128	        let (then_section, then_label) = self.reserve_next_section_label();
   129	        let (otherwise_section, otherwise_label) = self.reserve_next_section_label();
   130	        let (end_section, end_label) = self.reserve_next_section_label();
   131	
   132	        self.jump_if_instruction(condition, then_label);
   133	        self.jump_instruction(otherwise_label);
   134	
   135	        self.enter_section(then_section);
   136	        f(self, true);
   137	        self.jump_instruction(end_label);
   138	
   139	        self.enter_section(otherwise_section);
   140	        f(self, false);
   141	        // Fall through into `end_section`
   142	
   143	        self.enter_section(end_section);
   144	    }
   145	
   146	    /// This codegen issues a branch that jumps over the code generated by the given function if the condition is false
   147	    #[expect(unused)]
   148	    pub(crate) fn codegen_if(
   149	        &mut self,
   150	        condition: MemoryAddress,
   151	        f: impl FnOnce(&mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>),
   152	    ) {
   153	        let (end_section, end_label) = self.reserve_next_section_label();
   154	        let (then_section, then_label) = self.reserve_next_section_label();
   155	
   156	        self.jump_if_instruction(condition, then_label);
   157	        self.jump_instruction(end_label);
   158	
   159	        self.enter_section(then_section);
   160	        f(self);
   161	
   162	        self.enter_section(end_section);
   163	    }
   164	
   165	    /// This codegen issues a branch that jumps over the code generated by the given function if the condition is truthy
   166	    pub(crate) fn codegen_if_not(
   167	        &mut self,
   168	        condition: MemoryAddress,
   169	        f: impl FnOnce(&mut BrilligContext<F, Registers>),
   170	    ) {
   171	        let (end_section, end_label) = self.reserve_next_section_label();
   172	
   173	        self.jump_if_instruction(condition, end_label);
   174	
   175	        f(self);
   176	
   177	        self.enter_section(end_section);
   178	    }
   179	
   180	    /// Jump to a trap condition if `condition` is false.
   181	    /// The trap will include the given message as error data.
   182	    ///
   183	    /// If `error_selector` is None, an empty error data is generated (no error information).
   184	    pub(crate) fn codegen_constrain_with_error_data(
   185	        &mut self,
   186	        condition: SingleAddrVariable,
   187	        error_data_items: Vec<BrilligVariable>,
   188	        error_data_types: Vec<BrilligParameter>,
   189	        error_selector: Option<ErrorSelector>,
   190	    ) {
   191	        assert!(condition.bit_size == 1);
   192	
   193	        self.codegen_if_not(condition.address, |ctx| {
   194	            let data_size = Self::flattened_tuple_size(&error_data_types);
   195	
   196	            // Special case: No error selector means completely empty error data
   197	            let Some(error_selector) = error_selector else {
   198	                let error_data =
   199	                    ctx.make_usize_constant_instruction(0_usize.into()).map(|size| HeapVector {
   200	                        pointer: ReservedRegisters::free_memory_pointer(),
   201	                        size: size.address,
   202	                    });
   203	                ctx.trap_instruction(*error_data);
   204	                return;
   205	            };
   206	
   207	            // Shortcuts: empty data does not need without allocation, and can even use the procedure.
   208	            if data_size == 0 {
   209	                // use the procedure call for better code reuse
   210	                if ctx.can_call_procedures {
   211	                    if let Some(ErrorType::String(message)) =
   212	                        ctx.obj.error_types.get(&error_selector)
   213	                    {
   214	                        ctx.call_error_with_string_procedure(message.clone());
   215	                        return;
   216	                    }
   217	                }
   218	
   219	                // Fast path: Just write selector to free memory pointer, no allocation needed
   220	                ctx.indirect_const_instruction(
   221	                    ReservedRegisters::free_memory_pointer(),
   222	                    64,
   223	                    u128::from(error_selector.as_u64()).into(),
   224	                );
   225	                ctx.trap_instruction(HeapVector {
   226	                    pointer: ReservedRegisters::free_memory_pointer(),
   227	                    size: ReservedRegisters::usize_one(),
   228	                });
   229	                return;
   230	            }
   231	
   232	            // Allocate buffer and serialize data
   233	            // + 1 due to the error data id being the first item returned
   234	            let error_data_size = data_size + 1;
   235	            let error_data_size_var = ctx.make_usize_constant_instruction(error_data_size.into());
   236	            let error_data = ctx
   237	                .allocate_register()
   238	                .map(|pointer| HeapVector { pointer, size: error_data_size_var.address });
   239	            ctx.codegen_allocate_immediate_mem(error_data.pointer, error_data_size);
   240	
   241	            let current_error_data_pointer = ctx.allocate_register();
   242	            ctx.mov_instruction(*current_error_data_pointer, error_data.pointer);
   243	            ctx.indirect_const_instruction(
   244	                *current_error_data_pointer,
   245	                64,
   246	                u128::from(error_selector.as_u64()).into(),
   247	            );
   248	
   249	            ctx.codegen_usize_op_in_place(*current_error_data_pointer, BrilligBinaryOp::Add, 1);
   250	            for (error_variable, error_param) in
   251	                error_data_items.into_iter().zip(error_data_types.into_iter())
   252	            {
   253	                let flattened_size = Self::flattened_size(&error_param);
   254	                match error_param {
   255	                    BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(_) => {
   256	                        ctx.store_instruction(
   257	                            *current_error_data_pointer,
   258	                            error_variable.extract_single_addr().address,
   259	                        );
   260	                    }
   261	                    BrilligParameter::Array(item_type, item_count) => {
   262	                        let deflattened_items_pointer =
   263	                            ctx.codegen_make_array_items_pointer(error_variable.extract_array());
   264	
   265	                        ctx.flatten_array(
   266	                            &item_type,
   267	                            item_count,
   268	                            *current_error_data_pointer,
   269	                            *deflattened_items_pointer,
   270	                        );
   271	                    }
   272	                    BrilligParameter::Slice(_, _) => {
   273	                        unimplemented!("Slices are not supported as error data")
   274	                    }
   275	                }
   276	                ctx.codegen_usize_op_in_place(
   277	                    *current_error_data_pointer,
   278	                    BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   279	                    flattened_size,
   280	                );
   281	            }
   282	            ctx.trap_instruction(*error_data);
   283	        });
   284	    }

   286	    /// Jump to a trap condition if `condition` is false,
   287	    /// with any assertion message written to the error data.
   288	    pub(crate) fn codegen_constrain(
   289	        &mut self,
   290	        condition: SingleAddrVariable,
   291	        assert_message: Option<String>,
   292	    ) {
   293	        debug_assert!(condition.bit_size == 1);
   294	
   295	        // Compute error selector if we have a message
   296	        let error_selector = assert_message.map(|message| {
   297	            let error_type = ErrorType::String(message);
   298	            let error_selector = error_type.selector();
   299	            self.obj.error_types.insert(error_selector, error_type);
   300	            error_selector
   301	        });
   302	
   303	        self.codegen_constrain_with_error_data(
   304	            condition,
   305	            vec![], // No runtime data items
   306	            vec![], // No runtime data types
   307	            error_selector,
   308	        );
   309	    }
   310	
   311	    /// Computes the size of a parameter if it was flattened
   312	    pub(super) fn flattened_size(param: &BrilligParameter) -> usize {
   313	        match param {
   314	            BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(_) => 1,
   315	            BrilligParameter::Array(item_types, item_count)
   316	            | BrilligParameter::Slice(item_types, item_count) => {
   317	                let item_size: usize = item_types.iter().map(Self::flattened_size).sum();
   318	                item_count * item_size
   319	            }
   320	        }
   321	    }
   322	
   323	    /// Computes the size of a parameter if it was flattened
   324	    pub(super) fn flattened_tuple_size(tuple: &[BrilligParameter]) -> usize {
   325	        tuple.iter().map(Self::flattened_size).sum()
   326	    }
   327	
   328	    /// Computes the size of a parameter if it was flattened
   329	    pub(crate) fn has_nested_arrays(tuple: &[BrilligParameter]) -> bool {
   330	        tuple.iter().any(|param| !matches!(param, BrilligParameter::SingleAddr(_)))
   331	    }
   332	
   333	    // Flattens an array by recursively copying nested arrays and regular items.
   334	    pub(super) fn flatten_array(
   335	        &mut self,
   336	        item_type: &[BrilligParameter],
   337	        item_count: usize,
   338	        flattened_array_pointer: MemoryAddress,
   339	        deflattened_items_pointer: MemoryAddress,
   340	    ) {
   341	        if Self::has_nested_arrays(item_type) {
   342	            let movement_register = self.allocate_register();
   343	
   344	            let source_item_size = item_type.len();
   345	            let target_item_size: usize = item_type.iter().map(Self::flattened_size).sum();
   346	
   347	            for item_index in 0..item_count {
   348	                let source_item_base_index = item_index * source_item_size;
   349	                let target_item_base_index = item_index * target_item_size;
   350	
   351	                let mut target_offset = 0;
   352	
   353	                for (subitem_index, subitem) in item_type.iter().enumerate() {
   354	                    let source_index = self.make_usize_constant_instruction(
   355	                        (source_item_base_index + subitem_index).into(),
   356	                    );
   357	                    let target_index = self.make_usize_constant_instruction(
   358	                        (target_item_base_index + target_offset).into(),
   359	                    );
   360

   364	                                deflattened_items_pointer,
   365	                                *source_index,

   391	                            self.memory_op_instruction(
   392	                                flattened_array_pointer,

     1	use acvm::AcirField;
     2	
     3	use super::ProcedureId;
     4	use crate::brillig::brillig_ir::{
     5	    BrilligBinaryOp, BrilligContext,
     6	    brillig_variable::{BrilligVector, SingleAddrVariable},
     7	    codegen_memory::VectorMetaData,
     8	    debug_show::DebugToString,
     9	    registers::{RegisterAllocator, ScratchSpace},
    10	};
    11	
    12	impl<F: AcirField + DebugToString, Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligContext<F, Registers> {
    13	    /// Copy arguments to [ScratchSpace] and call [ProcedureId::VectorPopFront].
    14	    ///
    15	    /// Pops items from the front of a vector, returning the new vector.
    16	    /// The procedure assumes that there are constraints to prevent 0 size vectors from being popped.
    17	    pub(crate) fn call_vector_pop_front_procedure(
    18	        &mut self,
    19	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    20	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    21	        destination_vector: BrilligVector,
    22	        item_pop_count: usize,
    23	    ) {
    24	        let [
    25	            source_vector_length_arg,
    26	            source_vector_pointer_arg,
    27	            item_pop_count_arg,
    28	            destination_vector_pointer_return,
    29	        ] = self.make_scratch_registers();
    30	
    31	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_length_arg, source_len.address);
    32	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_pointer_arg, source_vector.pointer);
    33	        self.usize_const_instruction(item_pop_count_arg, item_pop_count.into());
    34	
    35	        self.add_procedure_call_instruction(ProcedureId::VectorPopFront);
    36	
    37	        self.mov_instruction(destination_vector.pointer, destination_vector_pointer_return);
    38	    }
    39	}
    40	
    41	/// Compile [ProcedureId::VectorPopFront].
    42	pub(super) fn compile_vector_pop_front_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
    43	    brillig_context: &mut BrilligContext<F, ScratchSpace>,
    44	) {
    45	    let [
    46	        source_vector_length_arg,
    47	        source_vector_pointer_arg,
    48	        item_pop_count_arg,
    49	        destination_vector_pointer_return,
    50	    ] = brillig_context.allocate_scratch_registers();
    51	
    52	    let source_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: source_vector_pointer_arg };
    53	    let target_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: destination_vector_pointer_return };
    54	
    55	    let VectorMetaData {
    56	        rc: source_rc,
    57	        size: source_size,
    58	        capacity: source_capacity,
    59	        items_pointer: source_items_pointer,
    60	    } = brillig_context.codegen_read_vector_metadata(
    61	        source_vector,
    62	        Some((source_vector_length_arg, item_pop_count_arg)),
    63	    );
    64	
    65	    // target_size = source_size - item_pop_count
    66	    // Assumes constraints exist against underflow.
    67	    // We don't have to worry about the semantic length of merged vectors here, because we are popping from the front.
    68	    let target_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    69	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    70	        source_size.address,
    71	        item_pop_count_arg,
    72	        target_size.address,
    73	        BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    74	    );
    75	
    76	    let is_rc_one = brillig_context.codegen_usize_equals_one(*source_rc);
    77	
    78	    brillig_context.codegen_branch(is_rc_one.address, |brillig_context, is_rc_one| {
    79	        if is_rc_one {
    80	            // We reuse the source vector, moving the metadata to the right (decreasing capacity)
    81	            // Set the target vector pointer to be the source plus the number of popped items.
    82	            brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    83	                source_vector.pointer,
    84	                item_pop_count_arg,
    85	                target_vector.pointer,
    86	                BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
    87	            );
    88	            // Decrease the source capacity by the number of popped items.
    89	            // This is done at the original address; it will be copied in the next step.
    90	            brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    91	                source_capacity.address,
    92	                item_pop_count_arg,
    93	                source_capacity.address,
    94	                BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    95	            );
    96	            // Re-initialize the metadata at the shifted position.
    97	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector_metadata(
    98	                target_vector,
    99	                *target_size,
   100	                *source_capacity,
   101	            );
   102	        } else {
   103	            // We can't reuse the source vector, so allocate a new one.
   104	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector(target_vector, *target_size, None);
   105	
   106	            let target_vector_items_pointer =
   107	                brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(target_vector);
   108	
   109	            // Set the source pointer to copy from to the source items start plus the number of popped items.
   110	            let source_copy_pointer = brillig_context.allocate_register();
   111	            brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   112	                source_items_pointer.address,
   113	                item_pop_count_arg,
   114	                *source_copy_pointer,
   115	                BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   116	            );
   117	            // Now we copy the source vector into the target vector, starting at index after the popped items.
   118	            brillig_context.codegen_mem_copy(
   119	                *source_copy_pointer,
   120	                *target_vector_items_pointer,
   121	                *target_size,
   122	            );
   123	            // We don't decrease the RC of the source vector, otherwise repeatedly popping the same item
   124	            // from the original (immutable) handle would bring its RC down to 1.
   125	        }
   126	    });
   127	}
   128

    27	/// Reference to an instruction
    28	///
    29	/// Note that InstructionIds are not unique. That is, two InstructionIds
    30	/// may refer to the same Instruction data. This is because, although
    31	/// identical, instructions may have different results based on their
    32	/// placement within a block.
    33	pub(crate) type InstructionId = Id<Instruction>;
    34	
    35	/// These are similar to built-ins in other languages.
    36	/// These can be classified under two categories:
    37	/// - Opcodes which the IR knows the target machine has
    38	///   special support for. (LowLevel)
    39	/// - Opcodes which have no function definition in the
    40	///   source code and must be processed by the IR.
    41	#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Hash, Serialize, Deserialize)]
    42	pub enum Intrinsic {
    43	    /// ArrayLen - returns the length of the input array
    44	    /// argument: array (value id)
    45	    /// result: length of the array, panic if the input is not an array
    46	    ArrayLen,
    47	    /// ArrayAsStrUnchecked - Converts a byte array of type `[u8; N]` to a string
    48	    /// argument: array (value id)
    49	    /// result: str
    50	    ArrayAsStrUnchecked,
    51	    /// AsSlice
    52	    /// argument: value id
    53	    /// result: a slice containing the elements of the argument. Panic if the value id does not correspond to an `array` type
    54	    AsSlice,
    55	    /// AssertConstant - Enforce the argument to be a constant value, at compile time.
    56	    /// argument: value id
    57	    /// result: (), panic if the argument does not resolve to a constant value
    58	    AssertConstant,
    59	    /// StaticAssert - Enforce the first argument to be true, at compile time
    60	    /// arguments: boolean (value id), ...message. The message can be a `format string` of several arguments
    61	    /// result: (), panic if the arguments do not resolve to constant values or if the first one is false.
    62	    StaticAssert,
    63	    /// SlicePushBack - Add elements at the end of a slice
    64	    /// arguments:  slice length, slice contents, ...elements_to_push
    65	    /// result: a slice containing `slice contents,..elements_to_push`
    66	    SlicePushBack,
    67	    /// SlicePushFront - Add elements at the start of a slice
    68	    /// arguments:  slice length, slice contents, ...elements_to_push
    69	    /// result: a slice containing `..elements_to_push, slice contents`
    70	    SlicePushFront,
    71	    /// SlicePopBack - Removes the last element of a slice
    72	    /// arguments: slice length, slice contents
    73	    /// result: a slice without the last element of `slice contents`
    74	    SlicePopBack,
    75	    /// SlicePopFront - Removes the first element of a slice
    76	    /// arguments: slice length, slice contents
    77	    /// result: a slice without the first element of `slice contents`
    78	    SlicePopFront,
    79	    /// SliceInsert - Insert elements inside a slice.
    80	    /// arguments: slice length, slice contents, insert index, ...elements_to_insert
    81	    /// result: a slice with ...elements_to_insert inserted at the `insert index`
    82	    SliceInsert,
    83	    /// SliceRemove - Removes an element from a slice
    84	    /// arguments: slice length, slice contents, remove index
    85	    /// result: a slice with without the element at `remove index`
    86	    SliceRemove,
    87	    /// ApplyRangeConstraint - Enforces the `bit size` of the first argument via a range check.
    88	    /// arguments: value id, bit size (constant)
    89	    /// result: applies a range check constraint to the input. It is replaced by a RangeCheck instruction during simplification.
    90	    ApplyRangeConstraint,
    91	    /// StrAsBytes - Convert a `str` into a byte array of type `[u8; N]`
    92	    /// arguments: value id
    93	    /// result: the argument. Internally a `str` is a byte array.
    94	    StrAsBytes,
    95	    /// ToBits(Endian) - Computes the bit decomposition of the argument.
    96	    /// argument: a field element (value id)
    97	    /// result: an array whose elements are the bit decomposition of the argument, in the endian order depending on the chosen variant.
    98	    /// The type of the result gives the number of limbs to use for the decomposition.
    99	    ToBits(Endian),
   100	    /// ToRadix(Endian) - Decompose the first argument over the `radix` base
   101	    /// arguments: a field element (value id), the radix to use (constant, a power of 2 between 2 and 256)
   102	    /// result: an array whose elements are the decomposition of the argument into the `radix` base, in the endian order depending on the chosen variant.
   103	    /// The type of the result gives the number of limbs to use for the decomposition.
   104	    ToRadix(Endian),
   105	    /// BlackBox(BlackBoxFunc) - Calls a blackbox function. More details can be found here: [acvm-repo::acir::::circuit::opcodes::BlackBoxFuncCall]
   106	    BlackBox(BlackBoxFunc),
   107	    /// Hint(Hint) - Avoid its arguments to be removed by DIE.
   108	    /// arguments: ... value id
   109	    /// result: the arguments. Hint does not layout any constraint but avoid its arguments to be simplified out during SSA transformations
   110	    Hint(Hint),
   111	    /// AsWitness - Adds a new witness constrained to be equal to the argument
   112	    /// arguments: value id
   113	    /// result: the argument
   114	    AsWitness,
   115	    /// IsUnconstrained - Indicates if the execution context is constrained or unconstrained
   116	    /// argument: ()
   117	    /// result: true if execution is under unconstrained context, false else.
   118	    IsUnconstrained,
   119	    /// DerivePedersenGenerators - Computes the Pedersen generators
   120	    /// arguments: domain_separator_string (constant string), starting_index (constant)
   121	    /// result: array of elliptic curve points (Grumpkin) containing the generators.
   122	    /// The type of the result gives the number of generators to compute.
   123	    DerivePedersenGenerators,
   124	    /// FieldLessThan - Compare the arguments: `lhs` < `rhs`
   125	    /// arguments: lhs, rhs. Field elements
   126	    /// result: true if `lhs` mod p < `rhs` mod p (p being the field characteristic), false else
   127	    FieldLessThan,
   128	    /// ArrayRefCount - Gives the reference count of the array
   129	    /// argument: array (value id)
   130	    /// result: reference count of `array`. In unconstrained context, the reference count is stored alongside the array.
   131	    /// in constrained context, it will be 0.
   132	    ArrayRefCount,
   133	    /// SliceRefCount - Gives the reference count of the slice
   134	    /// arguments: slice length, slice contents (value id)
   135	    /// result: reference count of `slice`. In unconstrained context, the reference count is stored alongside the slice.
   136	    /// in constrained context, it will be 0.
   137	    SliceRefCount,
   138	}

   171	
   172	impl Intrinsic {
   173	    /// Returns whether the `Intrinsic` has side effects.
   174	    ///
   175	    /// If there are no side effects then the `Intrinsic` can be removed if the result is unused.
   176	    ///
   177	    /// An example of a side effect is increasing the reference count of an array, but functions
   178	    /// which can fail due to implicit constraints are also considered to have a side effect.
   179	    pub(crate) fn has_side_effects(&self) -> bool {
   180	        match self {
   181	            Intrinsic::AssertConstant
   182	            | Intrinsic::StaticAssert
   183	            | Intrinsic::ApplyRangeConstraint
   184	            // Array & slice ref counts are treated as having side effects since they operate
   185	            // on hidden variables on otherwise identical array values.
   186	            | Intrinsic::ArrayRefCount
   187	            | Intrinsic::SliceRefCount
   188	            | Intrinsic::AsWitness => true,
   189	
   190	            // These apply a constraint that the input must fit into a specified number of limbs.
   191	            Intrinsic::ToBits(_) | Intrinsic::ToRadix(_) => true,
   192	
   193	            // These imply a check that the slice is non-empty and should fail otherwise.
   194	            Intrinsic::SlicePopBack | Intrinsic::SlicePopFront | Intrinsic::SliceRemove | Intrinsic::SliceInsert => true,
   195	
   196	            Intrinsic::ArrayLen
   197	            | Intrinsic::ArrayAsStrUnchecked
   198	            | Intrinsic::AsSlice
   199	            | Intrinsic::SlicePushBack
   200	            | Intrinsic::SlicePushFront

    11	impl<F: AcirField + DebugToString, Registers: RegisterAllocator> BrilligContext<F, Registers> {
    12	    /// Copy arguments to [ScratchSpace] and call [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    13	    ///
    14	    /// Pops `item_pop_count` items from the back of a `source_vector`, returning the new `destination_vector`
    15	    /// and the pointer to the popped items in `read_pointer`.
    16	    ///
    17	    /// The `item_pop_count` equals the number of variables to pop into in SSA.
    18	    /// The `source_len` is the semantic (not flattened) length of the vector.
    19	    pub(crate) fn call_vector_pop_back_procedure(
    20	        &mut self,
    21	        source_len: SingleAddrVariable,
    22	        source_vector: BrilligVector,
    23	        destination_vector: BrilligVector,
    24	        read_pointer: MemoryAddress,
    25	        item_pop_count: usize,
    26	    ) {
    27	        let [
    28	            source_vector_length_arg,
    29	            source_vector_pointer_arg,
    30	            item_pop_count_arg,
    31	            destination_vector_pointer_return,
    32	            read_pointer_return,
    33	        ] = self.make_scratch_registers();
    34	
    35	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_length_arg, source_len.address);
    36	        self.mov_instruction(source_vector_pointer_arg, source_vector.pointer);
    37	        self.usize_const_instruction(item_pop_count_arg, item_pop_count.into());
    38	
    39	        self.add_procedure_call_instruction(ProcedureId::VectorPopBack);
    40	
    41	        self.mov_instruction(destination_vector.pointer, destination_vector_pointer_return);
    42	        self.mov_instruction(read_pointer, read_pointer_return);
    43	    }
    44	}
    45	
    46	/// Compile [ProcedureId::VectorPopBack].
    47	pub(super) fn compile_vector_pop_back_procedure<F: AcirField + DebugToString>(
    48	    brillig_context: &mut BrilligContext<F, ScratchSpace>,
    49	) {
    50	    let [
    51	        source_vector_length_arg,
    52	        source_vector_pointer_arg,
    53	        item_pop_count_arg,
    54	        destination_vector_pointer_return,
    55	        read_pointer_return,
    56	    ] = brillig_context.allocate_scratch_registers();
    57	
    58	    let source_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: source_vector_pointer_arg };
    59	    let target_vector = BrilligVector { pointer: destination_vector_pointer_return };
    60	
    61	    // First we need to allocate the target vector decrementing the size by `item_pop_count`.
    62	    // We use the semantic length, rather than load the vector size from the meta-data,
    63	    // because after merging vectors of different lengths, the semantic length can be different
    64	    // then the number of items in the vector, which is the longer of the merged values.
    65	    let source_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    66	    brillig_context.codegen_vector_flattened_size(
    67	        source_size.address,
    68	        source_vector_length_arg,
    69	        item_pop_count_arg,
    70	    );
    71	
    72	    // We will pop a number of (flattened) items; targets_size = source_size - item_pop_count
    73	    let target_size = brillig_context.allocate_single_addr_usize();
    74	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
    75	        source_size.address,
    76	        item_pop_count_arg,
    77	        target_size.address,
    78	        BrilligBinaryOp::Sub,
    79	    );
    80	
    81	    let rc = brillig_context.codegen_read_vector_rc(source_vector);
    82	
    83	    let is_rc_one = brillig_context.codegen_usize_equals_one(*rc);
    84	
    85	    let source_vector_items_pointer =
    86	        brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(source_vector);
    87	
    88	    brillig_context.codegen_branch(is_rc_one.address, |brillig_context, is_rc_one| {
    89	        if is_rc_one {
    90	            // We can reuse the source vector, updating its length
    91	            brillig_context.mov_instruction(target_vector.pointer, source_vector.pointer);
    92	            brillig_context.codegen_update_vector_size(target_vector, *target_size);
    93	        } else {
    94	            // We need to clone the source vector; allocate memory for it.
    95	            brillig_context.codegen_initialize_vector(target_vector, *target_size, None);
    96	
    97	            let target_vector_items_pointer =
    98	                brillig_context.codegen_make_vector_items_pointer(target_vector);
    99	
   100	            // Now we copy the source vector starting at index 0 into the target vector but with the reduced length.
   101	            brillig_context.codegen_mem_copy(
   102	                *source_vector_items_pointer,
   103	                *target_vector_items_pointer,
   104	                *target_size,
   105	            );
   106	
   107	            // We don't decrease the RC of the source vector, otherwise repeatedly popping the same item
   108	            // from the original (immutable) handle would bring its RC down to 1.
   109	        }
   110	    });
   111	
   112	    // Finally set the pointer where the popped items can be read from to the source vector.
   113	    brillig_context.memory_op_instruction(
   114	        *source_vector_items_pointer,
   115	        target_size.address,
   116	        read_pointer_return,
   117	        BrilligBinaryOp::Add,
   118	    );
   119	}
   120
